<h1>Spanish Idioms </h1><img src="http://www.languagerealm.com/images/hr.png" style="padding-left:10px"><br><br>

<div style="text-align:center">

<script type="text/javascript"><!--

google_ad_client = "ca-pub-0582947305475738";

/* Languagerealm Main Top Banner */

google_ad_slot = "2103813162";

<img src="http://www.languagerealm.com/images/hr.png" style="padding-left:10px"><br>

<br>

  <p>Spanish idioms are essential to understanding and communicating with native speakers. Because Spanish is spoken in so many different countries, extra care is required when learning idioms. Make sure to pay attention to who is saying what under what circumstances before you attempt to use anything but the most common expression. Browse below to take a look at just how many different ways you can express yourself in Spanish.</p>

       <h2><a href="spanishidioms.php">A</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_b.php">B</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_c.php">C</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_d.php">D</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_e.php">E</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_f.php">F</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_g.php">G</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_h.php">H</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_i.php">I</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_j.php">J</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_l.php">L</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_m.php">M</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_n.php">N</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_o.php">O</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_p.php">P</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_q.php">Q</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_r.php">R</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_s.php">S</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_t.php">T</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_u.php">U</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_v.php">V</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_y.php">Y</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_z.php">Z</a></h2><br>

       <p><strong>a (la) merced de</strong><br>

at the mercy of (n.b.: the “la” is often omitted)</p>

<p><strong>a altas horas de la  madrugada</strong><br>

  in the small hours of the morning</p>

<p><strong>a cargo de</strong><br>

  in charge of; responsible for; by</p>

<p><strong>a causa de</strong><br>

  because of; as a result of (lit.: at the cause of)</p>

<p><strong>a chorros</strong><br>

  in abundance; plenty; lots</p>

<p><strong>a contrapelo</strong><br>

  wrong way; backwards; backassed</p>

<p><strong>a corto plazo</strong><br>

  in the short run; short-term; in the short term (lit.: at  short place)</p>

<p><strong>a deshora</strong><br>

  at an inconvenient time</p>

<p><strong>a diario</strong><br>

  daily; every day</p>

<p><strong>a disgusto</strong><br>

  reluctantly</p>

<p><strong>a duras penas</strong><br>

  hardly; barely; with difficulty</p>

<p><strong>a eso de</strong><br>

  around, about (time) (lit.: a this of)</p>

<p><strong>a estas alturas</strong><br>

  at this point; in this situation</p>

<p><strong>a fin de cuentas</strong><br>

  in the end; after all</p>

<p><strong>a fondo</strong><br>

  in depth; deeply; fully</p>

<p><strong>a gatas</strong><br>

  crawling (lit.: on legs/feet; used with the verbs estar or  andar)</p>

<p><strong>a juro</strong><br>

  no matter what (used in Venezuela)</p>

<p><strong>a la altura</strong><br>

  at the level; up to (lit.: at the height)</p>

<p><strong>a la intemperie</strong><br>

  in the open (lit.: at/on the elements. Intemperie refers to  the weather and other forces in the physical, natural world, particularly as  experienced without the benefits of technology, particularly modern technology)</p>

<p><strong>a la par de</strong><br>

  on the same level as</p>

<p><strong>a la salida del sol</strong><br>

  sunrise (lit.: at the appearance of the sun)</p>

<p><strong>a la vez</strong><br>

  at once; at the same time (lit.: at the time)</p>

<p><strong>a la vista</strong><br>

  in view; in sight (lit.: at the sight)</p>

<p><strong>a la vuelta</strong><br>

  on the way back (lit: at the turn)</p>

<p><strong>a la vuelta de</strong><br>

  just around the corner (lit.: at the turn of). 1. Mi  restaurante favorito está justo a la vuelta de mi oficina.</p>

<p><strong>a largo plazo</strong><br>

  in the long run; long-term; in the long term (lit.: at long  place)</p>

<p><strong>a lo largo (de)</strong><br>

  along; at the other end (lit.: at the far/long)</p>

<p><strong>a lo lejos</strong><br>

  from afar; at a distance (lit.: at the distant; allso in the  form “a los lejos.”)</p>

<p><strong>a lo mejor</strong><br>

  probably; most likely (lit.: to the better)</p>

<p><strong>a manos de</strong><br>

  at the hands of</p>

<p><strong>a manos llenas</strong><br>

  generously; lavishly (lit.: with full hands)</p>

<p><strong>a medida que</strong><br>

  as (something happens or happened); in the process of  (something happening)</p>

<p><strong>a medio plazo</strong><br>

  medium-term; in the medium term</p>

<p><strong>a menudo</strong><br>

  often, frequently (lit.: of often)</p>

<p><strong>a mi modo de pensar</strong><br>

  in my view; the way I see it</p>

<p><strong>a mi modo de ver</strong><br>

  in my view; the way I see it</p>

<p><strong>a otro perro con ese  hueso</strong><br>

  go tell it to the marines (lit.: [give] this bone to another  dog)</p>

<p><strong>a palo seco</strong><br>

  on its own; with nothing else</p>

<p><strong>a partir de ahora</strong><br>

  from now one (lit.: at the start of now)</p>

<p><strong>a pesar de</strong><br>

  despite; in spite of</p>

<p><strong>a plazo</strong><br>

  on credit</p>

<p><strong>a plena luz</strong><br>

  in broad daylight</p>

<p><strong>a primera hora</strong><br>

  at the earliest moment</p>

<p><strong>a primera vista</strong><br>

  at first sight; at first blush (lit.: at first sight)</p>

<p><strong>a propósito</strong><br>

  on purpose; deliberately</p>

<p><strong>a propósito</strong><br>

  by the way; speaking of which</p>

<p><strong>a punto de</strong><br>

  on the verge of, about to (lit.: at point of)</p>

<p><strong>a que</strong><br>

  I bet (lit.: to what)</p>

<p><strong>a ratos</strong><br>

  from time to time</p>

<p><strong>a sus espaldas</strong><br>

  behind someone's back</p>

<p><strong>a tientas</strong><br>

  by touch, by feel</p>

<p><strong>a toda costa</strong><br>

  at all costs (lit.: at all cost)</p>

<p><strong>a todo dar</strong><br>

  with full speed, far out, fabulous, great</p>

<p><strong>a toda máquina</strong><br>

  quickly, fast (lit.: at all machine)</p>

<p><strong>a toda prisa</strong><br>

  with all speed, hastily, quickly (lit.: at all haste)</p>

<p><strong>a todas luces</strong><br>

  by any reckoning</p>

<p><strong>a todo correr</strong><br>

  with all speed, hastily, quickly (lit.: at full running  (run))</p>

<p><strong>a toro pasado</strong><br>

  in retrospect; in hindsight (lit.: by the bull gone past)</p>

<p><strong>a trabajar</strong><br>

  to work (n.b.: said when encouraging yourself or others to  start working)</p>

<p><strong>a tráves de</strong><br>

  through</p>

<p><strong>a veces</strong><br>

  sometimes; at times</p>

<p><strong>a ver</strong><br>

  now then; let's see; hm-m</p>

<p><strong>a verga</strong><br>

  by hook or by crook</p>

<p><strong>a(l) fin de cuentas</strong><br>

  when all’s said and done; when it comes down to it (lit.: at  (the) end of accounts)</p>

<p><strong>ahora mismo</strong><br>

  right now; this minute</p>

<p><strong>al azar</strong><br>

  at random; randomly (lit.: to chance)</p>

<p><strong>al cabo de</strong><br>

  after, since (lit.: at the finish of)</p>

<p><strong>al fin y al cabo</strong><br>

  in the end; ultimately (lit.: at (the) end and at (the)  finish)</p>

<p><strong>al final</strong><br>

  in the end, finally (lit.: at (the) end)</p>

<p><strong>al menos</strong><br>

  at least, at a minimum (lit.: at the least)</p>

<p><strong>al oro</strong><br>

  good; well done (used in Venezuela)</p>

<p><strong>al parecer</strong><br>

  apparently; apparent; by appearances</p>

<p><strong>al pelo</strong><br>

just what is wanted or needed</p>

<p><strong>al poco rato</strong><br>

  after a little while</p>

<p><strong>al rape</strong><br>

  closely-cropped; close cut (lit.: to the monkfish)</p>

<p><strong>al revés</strong><br>

  backwards; the other way around; the opposite</p>

<p><strong>alcornoque</strong><br>

  blockhead; dunderhead; nincompoop (lit.: cork oak)</p>

<p><strong>almas gemelas</strong><br>

  soulmates (lit.: twin souls)</p>

<p><strong>andar a palos</strong><br>

  be fighting or squabbling all the time</p>

<p><strong>andar como burro sin  mecate</strong><br>

  be wild; be out of control (lit.: to walk like a donkey  wihout a leash)</p>

<p><strong>año nuevo, vida nueva</strong><br>

  Happy New Year (lit.: new year, new life; used as a greeting  or statement around Jan. 1)</p>

<p><strong>apalear oro</strong><br>

  be rolling in dough; be made of money</p>

<p><strong>apretarse el cinturón</strong><br>

  tighten one's belt; economize</p>

<p><strong>armar un jaleo</strong><br>

  make a fuss, commotion (lit.: to arm or raise a fuss)</p>

<p><strong>armar una bronca</strong><br>

  kick up a fuss</p>

<p><strong>armarse la gorda</strong><br>

  cause a ruckus; have all hell break loose (lit.: to arm  oneself the fat one)</p>

<p><strong>armarse un lio</strong><br>

  raise hell; make a fuss (lit.: to arm or raise a fight)</p>

<p><strong>arrimar el ascua a su  sardina</strong><br>

  put one’s own interests first; work things to one’s  advantage (lit.: to bring coals or embers to one’s sardine)</p>

<p><strong>así que</strong><br>

  so that, which means that (lit.: thus that)</p>

<p><strong>atar corto a alg</strong><br>

  keep someone on a short leash; keep someone under tight rein  (lit.: tie someone close)</p>

<p><strong>ausente sin culpa ni  presente sin disculpa</strong><br>

  the absentee is always in the wrong (lit.: absent without  blame and no present without excuses)</p>

<p><strong>Ave María Purísima</strong><br>

  for heaven’s sake (lit.: hail most pure Mary; n.b.: used in  religious services, and as an exclamation)</p><br>

<h1>Spanish Idioms </h1><img src="http://www.languagerealm.com/images/hr.png" style="padding-left:10px"><br><br>

<div style="text-align:center">

<script type="text/javascript"><!--

<img src="http://www.languagerealm.com/images/hr.png" style="padding-left:10px"><br>

<br>

  <p>Spanish idioms are essential to understanding and communicating with native speakers. Because Spanish is spoken in so many different countries, extra care is required when learning idioms. Make sure to pay attention to who is saying what under what circumstances before you attempt to use anything but the most common expression. Browse below to take a look at just how many different ways you can express yourself in Spanish.</p>

       <h2><a href="spanishidioms.php">A</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_b.php">B</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_c.php">C</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_d.php">D</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_e.php">E</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_f.php">F</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_g.php">G</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_h.php">H</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_i.php">I</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_j.php">J</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_l.php">L</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_m.php">M</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_n.php">N</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_o.php">O</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_p.php">P</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_q.php">Q</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_r.php">R</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_s.php">S</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_t.php">T</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_u.php">U</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_v.php">V</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_y.php">Y</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_z.php">Z</a></h2><br>

       <p><strong>bar de ligar</strong><br>

singles' bar; pickup joint (used in Spain)</p>

<p><strong>bicho raro</strong><br>

  oddball (lit.: rare bug)</p>

<p><strong>brillar por su  ausencia</strong><br>

  be conspicuous by one’s absence</p>

<p><strong>buscar bronca</strong><br>

  be spoiling for a fight; be looking for a fight</p><br>

<h1>Spanish Idioms </h1><img src="http://www.languagerealm.com/images/hr.png" style="padding-left:10px"><br><br>

<div style="text-align:center">

<script type="text/javascript"><!--

google_ad_client = "ca-pub-0582947305475738";

/* Languagerealm Main Top Banner */

google_ad_slot = "2103813162";

<img src="http://www.languagerealm.com/images/hr.png" style="padding-left:10px"><br>

<br>

  <p>Spanish idioms are essential to understanding and communicating with native speakers. Because Spanish is spoken in so many different countries, extra care is required when learning idioms. Make sure to pay attention to who is saying what under what circumstances before you attempt to use anything but the most common expression. Browse below to take a look at just how many different ways you can express yourself in Spanish.</p>

       <h2><a href="spanishidioms.php">A</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_b.php">B</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_c.php">C</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_d.php">D</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_e.php">E</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_f.php">F</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_g.php">G</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_h.php">H</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_i.php">I</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_j.php">J</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_l.php">L</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_m.php">M</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_n.php">N</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_o.php">O</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_p.php">P</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_q.php">Q</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_r.php">R</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_s.php">S</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_t.php">T</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_u.php">U</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_v.php">V</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_y.php">Y</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_z.php">Z</a></h2><br>

       <p><strong>cada hijo de vecino</strong><br>

every Tom, Dick, and Harry; everyone</p>

<p><strong>cada muerte de obispo</strong><br>

  once in a blue moon; very rarely (lit.: each time a bishop  dies)</p>

<p><strong>caer en la cuenta</strong><br>

  realize</p>

<p><strong>caer mal</strong><br>

  dislike; not like. 

  1. Me cae mal este  tipo.</p>

<p><strong>caerle bien a alguien</strong><br>

  look good; feel good; seem pleasant (lit.: to fall well to  someone)</p>

<p><strong>caérsele a alg la  baba con/por algo</strong><br>

  drool over someone or something; dote on someone; be crazy  about someone or something (lit.: to left fall slobber over someone or  something)</p>

<p><strong>caérsele los anillos  a algn</strong><br>

  be beneath one; be beneath one’s dignity (lit.: to have  one’s rings fall off)</p>

<p><strong>cambiar de idea</strong><br>

  change one’s mind (lit.: to change idea)</p>

<p><strong>cambiar de tema</strong><br>

  change a/the subject</p>

<p><strong>camino de</strong><br>

  along the way, on the way (lit.: road/path of)</p>

<p><strong>canta a pelo</strong><br>

sing unaccompanied</p>

<p><strong>carne de gallina</strong><br>

  gooseflesh</p>

<p><strong>cerrar algo a cal y  canto</strong><br>

  shut something tight, firmly, securely</p>

<p><strong>chiflar el moño a  algn</strong><br>

  be nuts; be crazy</p>

<p><strong>cielos</strong><br>

  heavens; oh my gosh (lit.: heavens; n.b.: used when  surprised, often in place of something vulgar)</p>

<p><strong>cien por cien</strong><br>

  100%; with certainty; precisely (lit.: one-hundred by  one-hundred)</p>

<p><strong>claro que sí</strong><br>

  of course; yes; indeed</p>

<p><strong>cocerse en un propia  salsa</strong><br>

  stew in one's (own) juice</p>

<p><strong>coger el toro por los  cuernos</strong><br>

  grab the bull by the horns (n.b.: coger is used only in  Spain)</p>

<p><strong>comer a deshora</strong><br>

  eat at odd times</p>

<p><strong>como agua para  chocolate</strong><br>

  furious; enraged (lit.: like water for chocolate)</p>

<p><strong>como de costumbre</strong><br>

  as usual (lit.: as of custom)</p>

<p><strong>como Dios manda</strong><br>

  the way it's supposed to be</p>

<p><strong>como perro en barrio  ajeno</strong><br>

  out of place; in the wrong neighborhood (lit.: like a dog in  a distant neighborhood; i.e.: people who try to enter other parts of society  may be attacked or ostracized)</p>

<p><strong>como quitarle un pelo  al gato</strong><br>

  a victimless crime (lit.: like removing a hair from a cat;  i.e.: the quantity in question is so small that it has no significant effect  and goes unnoticed)</p>

<p><strong>como si no fuera poco</strong><br>

  as if it were not enough</p>

<p><strong>como siempre</strong><br>

  as usual; as always</p>

<p><strong>como un oro</strong><br>

  like new (lit.: like a gold [coin])</p>

<p><strong>como un perro</strong><br>

  like a dog; like scum; in the gutter (lit.: like a dog)</p>

<p><strong>como una balsa de  aceite</strong><br>

  smoothly; swimmingly; peacefully (lit.: like a pool of oil)</p>

<p><strong>como una rosa</strong><br>

  fresh as a daisy; soft as silk (lit.: like a rose)</p>

<p><strong>con anticipación</strong><br>

  in advance; ahead of time</p>

<p><strong>con apuros</strong><br>

  with difficulty</p>

<p><strong>con pelos y señales</strong><br>

in minute detail; precisely</p>

<p><strong>con permiso</strong><br>

  with (your) permission</p>

<p><strong>con seguridad</strong><br>

  surely; certainly; absolutely</p>

<p><strong>con toda la barba</strong><br>

  real; the real deal; honest to goodness; true (lit.: with  all the beard)</p>

<p><strong>con todo respeto</strong><br>

  with all due respect. 

  1. Con todo respeto,  no me parece tan importante.</p>

<p><strong>consultarlo con la  almohada</strong><br>

  sleep on it (lit.: consult about something with the pillow)</p>

<p><strong>contar con</strong><br>

  count on</p>

<p><strong>correr la bola</strong><br>

  spread the word; put out the word</p>

<p><strong>cortar el bacalao</strong><br>

  call the shots (lit.: to cut the codfish; n.b.: Spain usage)</p>

<p><strong>cortar las alas a  alg.</strong><br>

  clip someone’s wings; nip something in the bud (lit.: cut  the wings of someone or something)</p>

<p><strong>cortar un pelo en el  aire</strong><br>

be smart</p>

<p><strong>corto de luces</strong><br>

  dim; dull; stupid</p>

<p><strong>cuando pueda</strong><br>

  when you can; when you have a moment</p>

<p><strong>cuanto antes</strong><br>

  as soon as possible (lit.: as much before)</p>

<p><strong>cuatro gatos</strong><br>

  a handful of people; half a dozen people; a small group of  people (lit.: four cats)</p><br>

<h1>Spanish Idioms </h1><img src="http://www.languagerealm.com/images/hr.png" style="padding-left:10px"><br><br>

<div style="text-align:center">

<script type="text/javascript"><!--

google_ad_client = "ca-pub-0582947305475738";

/* Languagerealm Main Top Banner */

google_ad_slot = "2103813162";

<img src="http://www.languagerealm.com/images/hr.png" style="padding-left:10px"><br>

<br>

  <p>Spanish idioms are essential to understanding and communicating with native speakers. Because Spanish is spoken in so many different countries, extra care is required when learning idioms. Make sure to pay attention to who is saying what under what circumstances before you attempt to use anything but the most common expression. Browse below to take a look at just how many different ways you can express yourself in Spanish.</p>

       <h2><a href="spanishidioms.php">A</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_b.php">B</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_c.php">C</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_d.php">D</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_e.php">E</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_f.php">F</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_g.php">G</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_h.php">H</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_i.php">I</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_j.php">J</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_l.php">L</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_m.php">M</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_n.php">N</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_o.php">O</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_p.php">P</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_q.php">Q</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_r.php">R</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_s.php">S</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_t.php">T</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_u.php">U</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_v.php">V</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_y.php">Y</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_z.php">Z</a></h2><br>

       <p><strong>dar a algn para el  pelo</strong><br>

be the living daylights out of someone; wipe the floor with  someone</p>

<p><strong>dar a entender</strong><br>

  let someone know</p>

<p><strong>dar a la luz</strong><br>

  give birth (lit.: to give to the light)</p>

<p><strong>dar la bienvenida</strong><br>

  welcome (lit.: to give the welcome)</p>

<p><strong>dar la lata</strong><br>

  be a nuisance; annoy (lit.: to give the tin)</p>

<p><strong>dar lástima</strong><br>

  make someone sad (to) (lit.: to give pain/sadness)</p>

<p><strong>dar luz verde</strong><br>

  give a green light to; permit; allow; clear</p>

<p><strong>dar muerte a</strong><br>

  kill someone</p>

<p><strong>dar nacimiento a</strong><br>

  give rise to</p>

<p><strong>dar palo</strong><br>

  hate; dislike; be unfortunate</p>

<p><strong>dar permiso</strong><br>

  permit; allow; give permission</p>

<p><strong>dar risa</strong><br>

  make one laugh; make one smile</p>

<p><strong>dar un paseo a  caballo</strong><br>

  go horseback riding; ride a horse</p>

<p><strong>dar un patatús a  alguien</strong><br>

  make someone have a fit (lit.: to give someone a fit)</p>

<p><strong>dar un salto</strong><br>

  jump; give a start; start (lit.: to give a jump)</p>

<p><strong>dar un vergajo</strong><br>

  screw; fuck; have sex with; shag</p>

<p><strong>dar una de cal y otra  de arena</strong><br>

  use a carrot-and-stick policy</p>

<p><strong>dar una fiesta</strong><br>

  give a party</p>

<p><strong>dar una vuelta</strong><br>

  go for a ride</p>

<p><strong>dar vida a</strong><br>

  portray; play (i.e.: an actor playing a role)</p>

<p><strong>darle a alguien mala  espina</strong><br>

  make someone feel uneasy (lit.: to give bad thorns to someone)</p>

<p><strong>darse cuenta de</strong><br>

  be aware; realize (lit.: to give oneself account of). 1. ¿Te  has dado cuenta de que en el supermercado tenemos hasta nueve tipos diferentes  de papel higiénico para elegir?</p>

<p>  <strong>darse por vencido</strong><br>

  give up; give in (lit.: to give oneself as defeated)</p>

<p><strong>darse prisa</strong><br>

  hurry; rush; do (something) fast (lit.: to give one urgency)</p>

<p><strong>de abrigo</strong><br>

  a handful; someone to watch out for (lit.: coat, overcoat)</p>

<p><strong>de ahí en adelante</strong><br>

  from now on; from here onward (lit.: from here in forward)</p>

<p><strong>de ahora en adelante</strong><br>

  from now on; henceforth; from this moment forward (lit.:  from now in advance)</p>

<p><strong>de armas tomar</strong><br>

  formidable; tough; redoubtable (lit.: for taking up arms)</p>

<p><strong>de buena gana</strong><br>

  willingly; with ease; with pleasure (lit.: of good desire)</p>

<p><strong>de buenas a primeras</strong><br>

  suddenly; without warning</p>

<p><strong>de cal y canto</strong><br>

  strong; firm</p>

<p><strong>de costumbre</strong><br>

  as usual; normally</p>

<p><strong>de cuando en cuando</strong><br>

  from time to time; sometimes; once in a while (lit.:&nbsp; of when in when)</p>

<p><strong>de diario</strong><br>

  everyday</p>

<p><strong>de golpe</strong><br>

  suddenly; abruptly; at once; all at once (lit.: of a blow or  strike)</p>

<p><strong>de hecho</strong><br>

  in fact, in reality (lit.: of fact). 1. De hecho, qiuero ir  contigo.</p>

<p>  <strong>de inmediato</strong><br>

  right now, immediately (lit.: from immediately)</p>

<p><strong>de medio pelo</strong><br>

second-rate</p>

<p><strong>de miedo</strong><br>

  fantastic(ally); wonderful(ly); brilliant(ly) (used in  Spain)</p>

<p><strong>de moda</strong><br>

  in fashion; in style</p>

<p><strong>de modo que</strong><br>

  so; so that</p>

<p><strong>de mucho cuidado</strong><br>

  big; terrible; real (used adverbially)</p>

<p><strong>de nada</strong><br>

  not at all; you’re welcome; don’t mention it (n.b.: often  said in response to “gracías”)</p>

<p><strong>de nuevo</strong><br>

  again; once again; anew (lit.: of new)</p>

<p><strong>de oro</strong><br>

  great; good; very good; wonderful. 

  1. Ella tiene una voz  de oro.</p>

<p><strong>de par en par</strong><br>

  wide open (lit.: from rafter to rafter)</p>

<p><strong>de pelo en pecho</strong><br>

manly; masculine</p>

<p><strong>de perlas</strong><br>

  just what someone needs; just right; go/fit perfectly (lit.:  of pearls)</p>

<p><strong>de perros</strong><br>

  foul; horrible; dirty</p>

<p><strong>de pocas luces</strong><br>

  dim; dull; stupid</p>

<p><strong>de pronto</strong><br>

  suddenly; at once; all at once (lit.: of soon)</p>

<p><strong>de repente</strong><br>

  abruptly, suddenly (lit.: of soon)</p>

<p><strong>de tal palo, tal  astilla</strong><br>

  like father, like son (lit.: of such a broom, such a  splinter)</p>

<p><strong>de todas maneras</strong><br>

  in any case; anyway</p>

<p><strong>de todos modos</strong><br>

  anyway; at any rate (lit.: to the monkfish)</p>

<p><strong>de un modo u otro</strong><br>

  one way or another</p>

<p><strong>de un momento a otro</strong><br>

  at any moment</p>

<p><strong>de una vez</strong><br>

  now</p>

<p><strong>de veras</strong><br>

  really, truly (lit.: of fact, truth)</p>

<p><strong>de vez en cuando</strong><br>

  sometimes; now and then (lit.: from once in when)</p>

<p><strong>decir amén a todo</strong><br>

  say yes to everything; agree to everything (lit.: to say  amen to everything)</p>

<p><strong>decir en broma</strong><br>

  kid; joke; tease (lit.: to say (as a) joke)</p>

<p><strong>dejar a alg en las  astas del toro</strong><br>

  leave someone high and dry; leave someone in the lurch  (lit.: to leave someone on the horns of the bull)</p>

<p><strong>dejar de lado</strong><br>

  set aside; put aside (lit.: to leave from (the) side)</p>

<p><strong>dejar en paz</strong><br>

  leave alone; leave be; let it be (lit.: to leave in peace)</p>

<p><strong>desde hacía rato</strong><br>

  for some time</p>

<p><strong>desde luego</strong><br>

  of course; certainly (lit.: after then/later)</p>

<p><strong>día a día</strong><br>

day after day. &nbsp;1. La  economía real, la que cada uno de nosotros maneja día a día es otra cosa. </p>

<p><strong>di que sí</strong><br>

  go for it (lit.: say yes)</p>

<p><strong>dormir el vino</strong><br>

  sleep off a hangover</p>

<p><strong>dormir juntos</strong><br>

  sleep together (n.b.: in the sexual sense)</p><br>

<h1>Spanish Idioms </h1><img src="http://www.languagerealm.com/images/hr.png" style="padding-left:10px"><br><br>

<div style="text-align:center">

<script type="text/javascript"><!--

<img src="http://www.languagerealm.com/images/hr.png" style="padding-left:10px"><br>

<br>

  <p>Spanish idioms are essential to understanding and communicating with native speakers. Because Spanish is spoken in so many different countries, extra care is required when learning idioms. Make sure to pay attention to who is saying what under what circumstances before you attempt to use anything but the most common expression. Browse below to take a look at just how many different ways you can express yourself in Spanish.</p>

       <h2><a href="spanishidioms.php">A</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_b.php">B</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_z.php">Z</a></h2><br>

       <p><strong>echar agua al vino</strong><br>

water down</p>

<p><strong>echar ajos y cebollas</strong><br>

  swear; curse; rant and rave (lit.: throw garlic and onions)</p>

<p><strong>echar de menos</strong><br>

  miss; feel the absence of (lit.: to throw less). 1. Puedes  pasar una temporada en un país extranjero sin echar de menos tu comida, tu ropa  o tú café favorito.</p>

<p><strong>echar el pelo</strong><br>

waste time (used in Cono del Sur)</p>

<p>  <strong>echar el toro a algn</strong><br>

  scold somebody severely (lit.: throw the bull to somebody)</p>

<p><strong>echar mano a</strong><br>

  lay hands on; get one's hands on</p>

<p><strong>echar mano de</strong><br>

  make use of; resort to</p>

<p><strong>echar por el atajo</strong><br>

  take the easy way out (lit.: throw for the shortcut)</p>

<p><strong>echar un mano</strong><br>

  help; assist (lit.: to throw less)</p>

<p><strong>echar un ojo a</strong><br>

  have one’s eye on; covet (lit.: to throw an eye at)</p>

<p><strong>echar un vistazo</strong><br>

  look around; glance; take a look (lit.: to throw less)</p>

<p><strong>echar una bronca</strong><br>

  hit hard; come down on</p>

<p><strong>echar una furia</strong><br>

  throw a fit</p>

<p><strong>echar una mano a algn</strong><br>

  let someone a hand; give someone a hand; help someone (lit.:  throw a hand to someone)</p>

<p><strong>echarle los perros a  algn</strong><br>

  come down hard on someone (lit.: throw dogs at someone)</p>

<p><strong>echarlo todo a rodar</strong><br>

  mess it all up; make a mess of everything</p>

<p><strong>echarse un novio/-a</strong><br>

  get a boy/girlfriend (used in Spain)</p>

<p><strong>el cuatro es nota, el  resto es lugo</strong><br>

  four is passing, anything else is a luxury (used in  Argentina)</p>

<p><strong>el pensamiento no  tiene/conoce barreras</strong><br>

  you can think whatever you like (lit.: thought does not  have/know barriers)</p>

<p><strong>el que se pica, ajos  come</strong><br>

  if the shoe fits, wear it</p>

<p><strong>el último grito</strong><br>

  the latest thing (lit.: the latest cry)</p>

<p><strong>en absoluto</strong><br>

  at all; (not) at all (usually used with a negative verb). 1.  No, en absoluto.</p>

<p>  <strong>en adelante</strong><br>

  from now on</p>

<p><strong>en bolas</strong><br>

  naked; nude; in the buff (Spain usage; lit: in balls)</p>

<p><strong>en bolas</strong><br>

  in a group; together (Mexican usage; lit.: in balls)</p>

<p><strong>en cambio</strong><br>

  on the other hand</p>

<p><strong>en carne viva</strong><br>

  in the flesh (lit.: in living meat)</p>

<p><strong>en carne viva</strong><br>

  raw; full; complete</p>

<p><strong>en carne y hueso</strong><br>

  in the flesh</p>

<p><strong>en caso de</strong><br>

  in case of; in case</p>

<p><strong>en cuanto a</strong><br>

  as for; when it comes to (lit.: in how much to). 1. En cuanto  a la comida, todo lo que preparan es riquísimo.</p>

<p>  <strong>en cuerpo y alma</strong><br>

  body and soul</p>

<p><strong>en definitiva</strong><br>

  in short; in brief</p>

<p><strong>en el acto</strong><br>

  in the act; red-handed</p>

<p><strong>en el medio de la  nada</strong><br>

  in the middle of nowhere (lit.: in the middle of (the)  nothing)</p>

<p><strong>en fin</strong><br>

  in short; in brief</p>

<p><strong>en lo más mínimo</strong><br>

  in the least bit</p>

<p><strong>en lugar de</strong><br>

  insted of, in place of (lit.: in place of)</p>

<p><strong>en manos de</strong><br>

  in the hands of</p>

<p><strong>en pie de</strong><br>

  on the verge of (lit.: at (the) foot of)</p>

<p><strong>en pos de</strong><br>

  in pursuit of; after</p>

<p><strong>en realidad</strong><br>

  actually; really; in reality</p>

<p><strong>en resumen</strong><br>

  in sum; in brief; briefly</p>

<p><strong>en seguida</strong><br>

  right away; at once; immediately</p>

<p><strong>en serio</strong><br>

  really, truly, seriously (lit.: in serious)</p>

<p><strong>en todo caso</strong><br>

  in any case; in any event; anyway</p>

<p><strong>en tu/su lugar</strong><br>

  in your/his/her place (lit.: in your/his/her place)</p>

<p><strong>en un abrir y cerrar  de ojos</strong><br>

  very quickly; in a flash; in the blink of an eye (lit.: in  the opening and closing of eyes.</p>

<p><strong>en un decir amén</strong><br>

  in a flash; in a jiffy; in next to no time (lit.: in the  saying of amen)</p>

<p><strong>en vez de</strong><br>

  instead of (lit.: in time of)</p>

<p><strong>entrar a hurtadillas</strong><br>

  sneak in</p>

<p><strong>entrar a saco</strong><br>

  burst in; storm in (lit.: to enter at sack)</p>

<p><strong>entrar bien</strong><br>

  go down well</p>

<p><strong>entrar de maravilla</strong><br>

  go down well</p>

<p><strong>entre algodones</strong><br>

  be pampered; be coddled (lit.: between cotton)</p>

<p><strong>entre bromas y veras</strong><br>

  half-joking(ly); half-serious(ly) (lit.: between jokes and  truths)</p>

<p><strong>entre manos</strong><br>

  on hand; at hand; immediately available</p>

<p><strong>es la salsa de la  vida</strong><br>

  it's the spice of life</p>

<p><strong>estallar en vivas</strong><br>

  burst into applause (lit.: to burst into lives)</p>

<p><strong>estar a cargo</strong><br>

  be in charge</p>

<p><strong>estar a dieta</strong><br>

  be on a diet (lit.: to be at diet)</p>

<p><strong>estar a disgusto</strong><br>

  be unhappy; be displeased</p>

<p><strong>estar a la miseria</strong><br>

  be in a bad way; be in a bad state</p>

<p><strong>estar a salvo</strong><br>

  be safe; be secure (lit.: to be at saved)</p>

<p><strong>estar a tope</strong><br>

  be very busy</p>

<p><strong>estar abocado al  frasco</strong><br>

  be doomed to failure</p>

<p><strong>estar al loro</strong><br>

  be on the alert; know the score (lit.: be at the parrot)</p>

<p><strong>estar al palo</strong><br>

  have an erection; be hard</p>

<p><strong>estar al tanto</strong><br>

  be abreast; be up to date (lit.: to be at the such)</p>

<p><strong>estar como agua para  chocolate</strong><br>

  be at the boiling point (lit.: like water for chocolate.  Indicates a boiling point of anger or passion. Note that this phrase was used  as the title for a movie, translated into English as “Like Water for  Chocolate.”)</p>

<p><strong>estar como el burro  del aguador; cargado de agua y muerto de sed</strong><br>

  not to see what's right before one's eyes (lit.: be like the  watercarrier's donkey; laden with water and dying of thirst; n.b.: a Mexican  expression)</p>

<p><strong>estar como las  propias rosas</strong><br>

  feel entirely at ease</p>

<p><strong>estar como tres en un  zapato</strong><br>

  be packed like sardines; be crammed in (lit.: be like three  in one shoe)</p>

<p><strong>estar con el agua al  cuello</strong><br>

  be up to one’s neck in problems; be over a barrel (lit.: be  with water at one’s collar)</p>

<p><strong>estar con el agua al  cuello</strong><br>

  be up to one's neck in something (lit.: have water up to  one's neck; n.b.: a Mexican saying)</p>

<p><strong>estar conforme</strong><br>

  be satisfied</p>

<p><strong>estar curtido en</strong><br>

  be expert at; be skilled at (lit.: be tanned, hardened in)</p>

<p><strong>estar de bromas</strong><br>

  be in a jokeing mood (lit.: to be for jokes)</p>

<p><strong>estar de buenas</strong><br>

  be in a good mood</p>

<p><strong>estar de juerga</strong><br>

  go out on the town; party; go clubbing</p>

<p><strong>estar de la cabeza</strong><br>

  be nuts; be insane</p>

<p><strong>estar de oferta</strong><br>

  be on sale; be discounted</p>

<p><strong>estar de Rodrígues</strong><br>

  be left on one's own (lit.: be Rodrigues; used in Spain)</p>

<p><strong>estar de siesta</strong><br>

  be on break; be on siesta</p>

<p><strong>estar de viaje</strong><br>

  be on vacation; be away (on vacation)</p>

<p><strong>estar de vuelta</strong><br>

  be back; have returned. 

  1. Ya estamos de  vuelta.</p>

<p>  <strong>estar del tomate</strong><br>

  be nuts; be insane (n.b.: not used much anymore)</p>

<p><strong>estar en ascuas</strong><br>

  be on pins and needles; be on tenerhooks (lit.: to be on  coals)</p>

<p><strong>estar en Babia</strong><br>

  have one’s head in the clouds (lit.: to be in Babia)</p>

<p><strong>estar en camino</strong><br>

  be on the way; be coming</p>

<p><strong>estar en el ajo</strong><br>

  be involved in; be mixed up in; be in the know (lit.: to be  in the garlic)</p>

<p><strong>estar en el orno</strong><br>

  be in a tight spot; be very anxious (used in Argentina)</p>

<p><strong>estar en juego</strong><br>

  be in play; be up for grabs (lit.: to be in play)</p>

<p><strong>estar en juego</strong><br>

  be at stake (lit.: to be in play)</p>

<p><strong>estar en la buena</strong><br>

  be in a good mood; be in luck (used in the Andes region)</p>

<p><strong>estar en la luna</strong><br>

  be on cloud nine; be out to lunch (lit.: to be on the moon)</p>

<p><strong>estar en la miseria</strong><br>

  be broke; be poor (used in Spain)</p>

<p><strong>estar en su salsa</strong><br>

  be in one's element</p>

<p><strong>estar harto de</strong><br>

  be fed up with; have had it with (lit.: to be exhausted). 1.  Estoy harto de esto.</p>

<p>  <strong>estar hasta el gorro</strong><br>

  be fed up; have had it (used in Spain)</p>

<p><strong>estar hasta el moño</strong><br>

  be fed up; have had it (used in Spain)</p>

<p><strong>estar hasta la  coronilla</strong><br>

  be fed up; have had it</p>

<p><strong>estar hasta las  narices</strong><br>

  be fed up; have had it (used in Spain)</p>

<p><strong>estar hasta los  cojones</strong><br>

  be fed up; have had it (vulgar)</p>

<p><strong>estar hecho un palo</strong><br>

  be as skinny as a rake; be very thin</p>

<p><strong>estar hecho una  flauta</strong><br>

  be thin as a rake (lit.: be like a flute)</p>

<p><strong>estar loco por algo</strong><br>

  be crazy for something; be nuts about something</p>

<p><strong>estar mal de dinero</strong><br>

  be hard up; have money problems</p>

<p><strong>estar mal de la  azotea</strong><br>

  be off one’s rocker; be nuts; be crazy (lit.: to be bad in  the roof)</p>

<p><strong>estar para el  arrastre</strong><br>

  be done in; be dead on one’s feet; have had it (lit.: to be  for dragging)</p>

<p><strong>estar pedo</strong><br>

  be sloshed; be drunk; be pissed; be high</p>

<p><strong>estar que arde</strong><br>

  be fuming; be hopping mad; be seething (lit.: to be that  which burns)</p>

<p><strong>estar seguro (de que)</strong><br>

  be sure; be certain (lit.: to be sure)</p>

<p><strong>estar sin animo</strong><br>

  be down; be in low spirits</p>

<p><strong>estar sin pasta</strong><br>

  be broke; be poor</p>

<p><strong>estar sin plata</strong><br>

  be broke; be poor</p>

<p><strong>estar sin un duro</strong><br>

  be broke; be poor (used in Spain)</p>

<p><strong>esto es el colmo</strong><br>

  that’s the last straw</p><br>

<h1>Spanish Idioms </h1><img src="http://www.languagerealm.com/images/hr.png" style="padding-left:10px"><br><br>

<div style="text-align:center">

<script type="text/javascript"><!--

<img src="http://www.languagerealm.com/images/hr.png" style="padding-left:10px"><br>

<br>

  <p>Spanish idioms are essential to understanding and communicating with native speakers. Because Spanish is spoken in so many different countries, extra care is required when learning idioms. Make sure to pay attention to who is saying what under what circumstances before you attempt to use anything but the most common expression. Browse below to take a look at just how many different ways you can express yourself in Spanish.</p>

       <h2><a href="spanishidioms.php">A</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_b.php">B</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_c.php">C</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_d.php">D</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_e.php">E</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_f.php">F</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_g.php">G</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_h.php">H</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_i.php">I</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_j.php">J</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_l.php">L</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_z.php">Z</a></h2><br>

       <p><strong>felices sueños</strong><br>

sweet dreams (lit.: happy dreams)</p>

<p><strong>florecer como rosa en  mayo</strong><br>

  blossom; flourish; bloom</p>

<p><strong>fuera de control</strong><br>

  out of control. 

  1. Nuestra casa está  fuera de control.</p>

<p><strong>fuera de duda</strong><br>

  certain; without doubt (lit.: outside of doubt)</p>

<p><strong>fuera de modo</strong><br>

  out of style; out of fashion</p>

<p><strong>fulano de tal</strong><br>

  somebody or other</p>

<p><strong>fulano, zutano y  mengano</strong><br>

  Tom, Dick, and Harry; everybody</p><br>

<h1>Spanish Idioms </h1><img src="http://www.languagerealm.com/images/hr.png" style="padding-left:10px"><br><br>

<br>

  <p>Spanish idioms are essential to understanding and communicating with native speakers. Because Spanish is spoken in so many different countries, extra care is required when learning idioms. Make sure to pay attention to who is saying what under what circumstances before you attempt to use anything but the most common expression. Browse below to take a look at just how many different ways you can express yourself in Spanish.</p>

beat someone to something (lit.: to win for oneself of/from  a hand)</p>

<p><strong>gastar una broma a  algn</strong><br>

  play a joke on; have fun at someone's expense</p><br>

  <p>Spanish idioms are essential to understanding and communicating with native speakers. Because Spanish is spoken in so many different countries, extra care is required when learning idioms. Make sure to pay attention to who is saying what under what circumstances before you attempt to use anything but the most common expression. Browse below to take a look at just how many different ways you can express yourself in Spanish.</p>

       <h2><a href="spanishidioms.php">A</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_b.php">B</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_c.php">C</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_d.php">D</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_z.php">Z</a></h2><br>

       <p><strong>haberse de sentar</strong><br>

hit the spot; agree with (someone)</p>

<p><strong>hablar de</strong><br>

  talk about</p>

<p><strong>hablar de bueyes  perdidos</strong><br>

  waste one's breath; chat about little things (n.b.: used in  Cono del Sur)</p>

<p><strong>hacer alharacas</strong><br>

  make a fuss; make a big deal about (lit.: to make a fuss)</p>

<p><strong>hacer caso</strong><br>

  pay attention to (lit.: to make a case)</p>

<p><strong>hacer chapuzas</strong><br>

  do odd jobs; do occasional work</p>

<p><strong>hacer compras</strong><br>

  shop; do (the) shopping (lit.: to make/do purchases)</p>

<p><strong>hacer coro a algn</strong><br>

  back someone up</p>

<p><strong>hacer del cuerpo</strong><br>

  defecate; move one's bowels (n.b.: euphemism)</p>

<p><strong>hacer el amor con</strong><br>

  make love with someone</p>

<p><strong>hacer el favor</strong><br>

  do a favor (lit.: to do the favor. Note that this can, as in  English, be used to give someone a command or order)</p>

<p><strong>hacer el sol</strong><br>

  the sun rises (lit.: to make the sun)</p>

<p><strong>hacer falta</strong><br>

  be necessary; must (lit.: to do the lack)</p>

<p><strong>hacer fiaca</strong><br>

  sleep in; stay home for the peace and quiet (used in  Argentina)</p>

<p><strong>hacer frente</strong><br>

  confront (lit.: to do the front)</p>

<p><strong>hacer la barba a alg</strong><br>

  suck up to someone; butter someone up (lit.: to do the beard  to someone)</p>

<p><strong>hacer la compra</strong><br>

  do the shopping; buy groceries</p>

<p><strong>hacer la cusqui</strong><br>

  bug; annoy; irritate</p>

<p><strong>hacer la vista gorda</strong><br>

  ignore; overlook (lit.: to do the fat look. The idea here  being of indulgence, the way a parent or grandparent might look at a  misbehaving child)</p>

<p><strong>hacer las compras</strong><br>

  do the shopping</p>

<p><strong>hacer las maletas</strong><br>

  pack; pack a suitcase (lit.: to do the suitcases)</p>

<p><strong>hacer las paces</strong><br>

  make up; make peace (lit.: to make the peace(s))</p>

<p><strong>hacer pucheros</strong><br>

  pout; screw up one's face</p>

<p><strong>hacer su agosto</strong><br>

  make a killing; make serious coin; hit the jackpot (lit.: to  make/do one’s August)</p>

<p><strong>hacer toros</strong><br>

  cut class; skip class (lit.: to the bulls)</p>

<p><strong>hacer trampa(s)</strong><br>

  cheat (lit.: to do traps)</p>

<p><strong>hacer un papel</strong><br>

  play a role; play a part</p>

<p><strong>hacer un papelón</strong><br>

  make a fool of oneself; embarras oneself (lit.: to make a  large role)</p>

<p><strong>hacer un simpa</strong><br>

  leave a restaurant without paying</p>

<p><strong>hacer un toro</strong><br>

  stand in for somebody (in a theatrical production) (lit.: to  do the bull)</p>

<p><strong>hacerle frente a alguien</strong><br>

  face someone (lit.: to make facing to someone)</p>

<p><strong>hacer a pelo y pluma</strong><br>

be AC/DC</p>

<p><strong>hacerse cargo de</strong><br>

  take charge of; pay for; realize</p>

<p><strong>hacerse ilusiones</strong><br>

  get one's hopes up</p>

<p><strong>hasta donde</strong><br>

  as far as (lit.: up to when)</p>

<p><strong>hecho una hiena</strong><br>

  furious; enraged</p>

<p><strong>hija de papá</strong><br>

  rich kid; rich girl</p>

<p><strong>hijo de papá</strong><br>

  rich kid; rich boy</p>

<p><strong>hoy mismo</strong><br>

  today. 

  1. Hazlo hoy mismo.</p><br>

<h1>Spanish Idioms </h1><img src="http://www.languagerealm.com/images/hr.png" style="padding-left:10px"><br><br>

<div style="text-align:center">

<script type="text/javascript"><!--

google_ad_client = "ca-pub-0582947305475738";

<img src="http://www.languagerealm.com/images/hr.png" style="padding-left:10px"><br>

<br>

  <p>Spanish idioms are essential to understanding and communicating with native speakers. Because Spanish is spoken in so many different countries, extra care is required when learning idioms. Make sure to pay attention to who is saying what under what circumstances before you attempt to use anything but the most common expression. Browse below to take a look at just how many different ways you can express yourself in Spanish.</p>

       <h2><a href="spanishidioms.php">A</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_b.php">B</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_c.php">C</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_d.php">D</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_e.php">E</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_f.php">F</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_g.php">G</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_h.php">H</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_i.php">I</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_j.php">J</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_l.php">L</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_m.php">M</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_n.php">N</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_o.php">O</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_p.php">P</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_q.php">Q</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_r.php">R</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_s.php">S</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_t.php">T</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_u.php">U</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_v.php">V</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_y.php">Y</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_z.php">Z</a></h2><br>

       <p><strong>ir a golpe de  alpargata</strong><br>

walk; hoof it; go on foot (lit.: go by slapping sandals)</p>

<p><strong>ir a medias</strong><br>

  go Dutch; go fifty-fifty (used in Spain)</p>

<p><strong>ir a pelo</strong><br>

be naked</p>

<p><strong>ir de compras</strong><br>

  go shopping</p>

<p><strong>ir de juerga</strong><br>

  go out on the town; party; go clubbing</p>

<p><strong>ir de marcha</strong><br>

  go out partying</p>

<p><strong>ir de tiendas</strong><br>

  go shopping (used in Spain)</p>

<p><strong>irse a la cabeza del  toro</strong><br>

  grab the bull by the horns</p>

<p><strong>irse al otro barrio</strong><br>

  kick the bucket (lit.: to go to another neighborhood)</p><br>

<h1>Spanish Idioms </h1><img src="http://www.languagerealm.com/images/hr.png" style="padding-left:10px"><br><br>

<div style="text-align:center">

<script type="text/javascript"><!--

<br>

  <p>Spanish idioms are essential to understanding and communicating with native speakers. Because Spanish is spoken in so many different countries, extra care is required when learning idioms. Make sure to pay attention to who is saying what under what circumstances before you attempt to use anything but the most common expression. Browse below to take a look at just how many different ways you can express yourself in Spanish.</p>

       <h2><a href="spanishidioms.php">A</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_b.php">B</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_c.php">C</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_d.php">D</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_e.php">E</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_f.php">F</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_g.php">G</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_h.php">H</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_i.php">I</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_j.php">J</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_l.php">L</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_m.php">M</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_n.php">N</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_o.php">O</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_p.php">P</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_q.php">Q</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_r.php">R</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_s.php">S</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_t.php">T</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_u.php">U</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_v.php">V</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_y.php">Y</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_z.php">Z</a></h2><br>

       <p><strong>la gran flauta</strong><br>

my God! (used to express surprise or disbelief)</p>

<p><strong>ladrar a la luna</strong><br>

  waste one’s breath; talk to a brick wall (lit.: to bark at  the moon)</p>

<p><strong>llegar a deshora</strong><br>

  show up unexpectedly</p>

<p><strong>llegar a tiempo</strong><br>

  arrive on time; be on time</p>

<p><strong>llegar a un acuerdo</strong><br>

  come to an agreement; reach an agreement</p>

<p><strong>llegar tarde</strong><br>

  arrive late; be late</p>

<p><strong>llevar a alguien en  andas</strong><br>

  carry someone on one’s shoulders (lit.: to carry someone on  a portable platform. An “andas” literally refers to a portable platform)</p>

<p><strong>llevar a cabo</strong><br>

  carry out; pull off; make happen (lit.: to carry to end). 1. Tendremos una reuníon esta tarde para discutir el 

  tipo de sociedad que formaríamos en el caso de que<br>

  decidamos llevarlo a cabo.</p>

<p><strong>llevar juntos</strong><br>

  be together; be involved; be a couple</p>

<p><strong>llevarse bien</strong><br>

  get along well</p>

<p><strong>llevarse de miedo</strong><br>

  get along famously; get along really well</p>

<p><strong>lo antes possible</strong><br>

  as soon as possible</p>

<p><strong>los de arriba</strong><br>

  the people on top; the upper crust (lit.: those above)</p>

<p><strong>los pros y las  contras</strong><br>

  the pros and the cons</p>

<p><strong>lotería</strong><br>

  bingo; got it (n.b.: said when finding something or  experiencing a stroke of good luck)</p><br>

<a href="spanishidioms_g.php">G</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_j.php">J</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_l.php">L</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_n.php">N</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_o.php">O</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_t.php">T</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_u.php">U</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_v.php">V</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_y.php">Y</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_z.php">Z</a></h2><br>

       <p><strong>maldita sea</strong><br>

damn it; darn it (lit.: may it be damned)</p>

<p><strong>mandar a paseo</strong><br>

  tell someone to take a hike</p>

<p><strong>mande</strong><br>

  what; please; how's that (used in Mexico as we in English  say "what" when we want someone to repeat or clarify something)</p>

<p><strong>mantener a raya</strong><br>

  keep someone at bay; keep someone away</p>

<p><strong>mantenerse en su  sitio</strong><br>

  stick to one's guns; stand one's ground (lit.: maintain  oneself in one's position)</p>

<p><strong>mantenerse en sus  trece</strong><br>

  stick to one's guns; stand one's ground (lit.: maintain  oneself in one's thirteen)</p>

<p><strong>mas o menos</strong><br>

  more or less; roughly; approximately (lit.: more or less)</p>

<p><strong>más tieso que un palo</strong><br>

  straight; upright; bolt upright</p>

<p><strong>mayor de edad</strong><br>

  of age</p>

<p><strong>media naranja</strong><br>

  better half; spouse, wife, partner (lit.: half of an orange)</p>

<p><strong>media pila</strong><br>

  minimal effort; some effort; enough effort to accomplish  something but no more (lit.: half a battery)</p>

<p><strong>menor de edad</strong><br>

  underage</p>

<p><strong>menos mal</strong><br>

  just as well, good thing, thank goodness (lit.: less bad)</p>

<p><strong>meter en líos</strong><br>

  get into trouble (lit.: to put into trouble)</p>

<p><strong>meter palos en las  ruedas</strong><br>

  throw a (monkey) wrench in the works; throw a spanner in the  works</p>

<p><strong>meter(se) la pata</strong><br>

  get involved; become a part of (lit.: to put in the leg  (animal’s paw))</p>

<p><strong>metete un pelo en el  culo</strong><br>

  stick it up your ass</p>

<p><strong>mi/tu abuela</strong><br>

  my foot (lit.: grandmother)</p>

<p><strong>mientras tanto</strong><br>

  meanwhile, in the meantime (lit.: to the monkfish)</p>

<p><strong>mirar de reojo</strong><br>

  look at out of the corner of the eye</p>

<p><strong>mirar por encima</strong><br>

  glance at; look quickly through</p>

<p><strong>momento</strong><br>

  wait; wait a second; wait a moment (used when asking someone  to wait briefly)</p>

<p><strong>montar a pelo</strong><br>

ride bareback</p>

<p><strong>montar un negocio</strong><br>

  set up a business; start a business (used in Spain)</p>

<p><strong>morirse de risa</strong><br>

  die laughing</p>

<p><strong>mostrar tino</strong><br>

  show good sense; be right (lit.: to show sound judgment,  good sense)</p><br>

<h1>Spanish Idioms </h1><img src="http://www.languagerealm.com/images/hr.png" style="padding-left:10px"><br><br>

<div style="text-align:center">

<script type="text/javascript"><!--

google_ad_client = "ca-pub-0582947305475738";

<img src="http://www.languagerealm.com/images/hr.png" style="padding-left:10px"><br>

<br>

  <p>Spanish idioms are essential to understanding and communicating with native speakers. Because Spanish is spoken in so many different countries, extra care is required when learning idioms. Make sure to pay attention to who is saying what under what circumstances before you attempt to use anything but the most common expression. Browse below to take a look at just how many different ways you can express yourself in Spanish.</p>

       <h2><a href="spanishidioms.php">A</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_b.php">B</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_c.php">C</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_d.php">D</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_e.php">E</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_f.php">F</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_g.php">G</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_h.php">H</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_i.php">I</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_j.php">J</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_l.php">L</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_m.php">M</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_n.php">N</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_o.php">O</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_p.php">P</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_q.php">Q</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_r.php">R</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_s.php">S</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_t.php">T</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_u.php">U</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_v.php">V</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_y.php">Y</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_z.php">Z</a></h2><br>

       <p><strong>nada del otro mundo</strong><br>

nothing special</p>

<p><strong>nadar en la  abundancia</strong><br>

  be rolling in dough; be made of money (lit.: to swim in  abundance)</p>

<p><strong>necesitar como agua de  mayo</strong><br>

  absolutely need something; really need something; must have  something</p>

<p><strong>ni a palos</strong><br>

  no way; not on your life</p>

<p><strong>ni en broma</strong><br>

  no way; not on your life (lit.: not even as a joke)</p>

<p><strong>ni pizca de</strong><br>

  not even a shred of (lit.: not even a pinch of)</p>

<p><strong>ni rastro</strong><br>

  no sign; no hint (of something)</p>

<p><strong>no abrir la bolsa</strong><br>

  be tight with money;</p>

<p><strong>no caber ni un  alfiler</strong><br>

  be completely packed; be jammed; be stuffed (lit.: no even  fit in a pin)</p>

<p><strong>no caérsele los  anillos a algn</strong><br>

  not to be beneath one; not be beneath one’s dignity (lit.: to  not have one’s rings fall off)</p>

<p><strong>no dar ni golpe</strong><br>

  do nothing; not do anything; be idle</p>

<p><strong>no es cosa mía</strong><br>

  it’s not my business; it’s not my affair</p>

<p><strong>no estar para bromas</strong><br>

  be in no mood for jokes (lit.: not to be for jokes)</p>

<p><strong>no importar un ardite</strong><br>

  could not care less; not give a hoot/damn (lit.: not be  worth an “ardite,” an old coin of little value)</p>

<p><strong>no llevar nada encima</strong><br>

  not have any money with</p>

<p><strong>no necesitar abuela</strong><br>

  be full of oneself; blow one’s own horn (lit.: not to have a  grandmother)</p>

<p><strong>no pararse en barras</strong><br>

  stop at nothing (lit.: not to stop at the bars [laws])</p>

<p><strong>no pasa nada</strong><br>

  no problem; not big deal</p>

<p><strong>no poder con su alma</strong><br>

  be exhausted; be fed up; be unable to take it anymore (lit.:  not to be able with one’s soul)</p>

<p><strong>no se oía ni una  mosca</strong><br>

  you could have heard a pin drop (lit.: no even a fly could  be heard)</p>

<p><strong>no ser ni carne ni  pescado</strong><br>

  be neither one thing nor the other (lit.: not be fish or  fowl)</p>

<p><strong>no tener abuela</strong><br>

  be full of oneself; blow one’s own horn (lit.: not to have a  grandmother)</p>

<p><strong>no tener arte ni  parte</strong><br>

  have nothing to do with something at all (lit.: not to have  art or part)</p>

<p><strong>no tener pelos en la  lengua</strong><br>

not mince words; be a straight shooter</p>

<p><strong>no tiene caso</strong><br>

  it is completely pointless; it is a waste of time</p>

<p><strong>no ver el pelo a algn</strong><br>

not see hide or hair of someone</p>

<p><strong>nunca se sabe</strong><br>

  you never know; you never can tell</p><br>

  <p>Spanish idioms are essential to understanding and communicating with native speakers. Because Spanish is spoken in so many different countries, extra care is required when learning idioms. Make sure to pay attention to who is saying what under what circumstances before you attempt to use anything but the most common expression. Browse below to take a look at just how many different ways you can express yourself in Spanish.</p>

<h1>Spanish Idioms </h1><img src="http://www.languagerealm.com/images/hr.png" style="padding-left:10px"><br><br>

<div style="text-align:center">

<script type="text/javascript"><!--

<br>

  <p>Spanish idioms are essential to understanding and communicating with native speakers. Because Spanish is spoken in so many different countries, extra care is required when learning idioms. Make sure to pay attention to who is saying what under what circumstances before you attempt to use anything but the most common expression. Browse below to take a look at just how many different ways you can express yourself in Spanish.</p>

       <h2><a href="spanishidioms.php">A</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_b.php">B</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_c.php">C</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_d.php">D</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_e.php">E</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_f.php">F</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_g.php">G</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_h.php">H</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_i.php">I</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_j.php">J</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_l.php">L</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_m.php">M</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_n.php">N</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_o.php">O</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_p.php">P</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_q.php">Q</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_r.php">R</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_s.php">S</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_t.php">T</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_u.php">U</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_v.php">V</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_y.php">Y</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_z.php">Z</a></h2><br>

       <p><strong>pagar a plazos</strong><br>

pay for something in installments</p>

<p><strong>para colmo de  desgracias</strong><br>

  to top it all; to top it off (lit.: for the height of  disgrace)</p>

<p><strong>para colmo de males</strong><br>

  to make matters worse</p>

<p><strong>para diario</strong><br>

  everyday</p>

<p><strong>parecer otro/-a</strong><br>

  look great; look fantastic</p>

<p><strong>partirse el alma</strong><br>

  make someone’s heart bleed (lit.: my soul is separated from  me)</p>

<p><strong>pasar a buscar</strong><br>

  pick up; collect; get</p>

<p><strong>pasar de la raya</strong><br>

  cross the line (lit.: to pass over the line)</p>

<p><strong>pasar el mono a pelo</strong><br>

go cold turky</p>

<p><strong>pasar por alto</strong><br>

  pass over; overlook; ignore (lit.: to pass by high)</p>

<p><strong>pasarlo bomba</strong><br>

  have a great time (lit.: to pass the bomb)</p>

<p><strong>pedir la luna</strong><br>

  ask the impossible (lit.: to ask for the moon)</p>

<p><strong>pegar el ojo</strong><br>

  fall asleep; sleep (lit.: to stick the eye)</p>

<p><strong>perder la cabeza</strong><br>

  fall madly in love with someone</p>

<p><strong>pez gordo</strong><br>

  fat cat; big cheese; big cheese (lit.: fat fish)</p>

<p><strong>poner a salvo</strong><br>

  save; rescue (lit.: to put to saving)</p>

<p><strong>poner el dedo en la  llaga</strong><br>

  hit a raw nerve (lit.: to put the finger in the ulcer)</p>

<p><strong>poner en camino</strong><br>

  get underway; be underway (lit.: to put onself on road, on  route)</p>

<p><strong>poner en cintura</strong><br>

  reign in (lit.: to put a belt on)</p>

<p><strong>poner en marcha</strong><br>

  start; begin; put into action</p>

<p><strong>poner en su sitio a  alguien</strong><br>

  put someone in his/her place (lit.: to place someone in  her/his site)</p>

<p><strong>poner la mesa</strong><br>

  set the table</p>

<p><strong>poner mala cara</strong><br>

  pout; grimace; give a dirty luck</p>

<p><strong>poner toda la carne  en el asador</strong><br>

  pull out all the stops</p>

<p><strong>ponerse a dieta</strong><br>

  go on a diet</p>

<p><strong>ponerse como una  hiena</strong><br>

  get pissed; be furious; hit the roof</p>

<p><strong>ponerse de acuerdo</strong><br>

  agree; come to an agreement</p>

<p><strong>ponerse de novio</strong><br>

  have a relationship; be serious with somebody</p>

<p><strong>ponerse de pie</strong><br>

  stand up (lit.: to put oneself on foot)</p>

<p><strong>ponerse en contra</strong><br>

  be against; protest; stand against</p>

<p><strong>ponerse las pilas</strong><br>

  force oneself; push oneself (lit.: put batteries in oneself)</p>

<p><strong>ponerse pedo</strong><br>

  get drunk; get sloshed; get pissed; get high</p>

<p><strong>por (el) amor de Dios</strong><br>

  for the love of God (n.b.: exclamation similar to the one in  English in usage)</p>

<p><strong>por adelantado</strong><br>

  early, beforehand (lit.: by earliness)</p>

<p><strong>por casualidad</strong><br>

  by coincidence, by any chance (lit.: by coincidence)</p>

<p><strong>por cierto</strong><br>

  by the way; incidentally</p>

<p><strong>por debajo de agua</strong><br>

  under the table</p>

<p><strong>por el contrario</strong><br>

  on the contrary (lit.: by its sight)</p>

<p><strong>por el momento</strong><br>

  for now (lit.: by the moment)</p>

<p><strong>por el otro lado</strong><br>

  on the other hand</p>

<p><strong>por eso</strong><br>

  so; thus; then; next</p>

<p><strong>por estos rumbos</strong><br>

  in this neck of the woods; around here</p>

<p><strong>por fin</strong><br>

  finally</p>

<p><strong>por fortuna</strong><br>

  fortunately</p>

<p><strong>por la buena</strong><br>

  nicely; without being forced</p>

<p><strong>por la flauta</strong><br>

  oh dear! (used to express surprise or frustration)</p>

<p><strong>por la mala</strong><br>

  only when pushed; only when forced</p>

<p><strong>por la verga grande</strong><br>

  in the back of beyond; in the sticks; in the boonies  (coarse, vulgar expression)</p>

<p><strong>por lo general</strong><br>

  generally; in general</p>

<p><strong>por lo menos</strong><br>

  at least; at a minimum (lit.: at/by the least)</p>

<p><strong>por lo pronto</strong><br>

  in the meantime; meanwhile. 1. Vea, por lo pronto existe una tercera opcíon.</p>

<p><strong>por lo regular</strong><br>

  normally</p>

<p><strong>por lo tanto</strong><br>

  thus; therefore (lit.: by its sight)</p>

<p><strong>por lo visto</strong><br>

  apparently; it seems (lit.: by its sight)</p>

<p><strong>por los pelos</strong><br>

by the skin of one's teeth</p>

<p><strong>por menos de nada</strong><br>

  for nothing; for less than nothing</p>

<p><strong>por otra parte</strong><br>

  on the other hand</p>

<p><strong>por pedido de</strong><br>

  at the request of</p>

<p><strong>por si acaso</strong><br>

  just in case</p>

<p><strong>por si fuera poco</strong><br>

  to add insult to injury</p>

<p><strong>por si las moscas</strong><br>

  just in case</p>

<p><strong>por siempre</strong><br>

  forever (lit.: for always)</p>

<p><strong>por suerte</strong><br>

  luckily, fortunately (lit.: by luck)</p>

<p><strong>por supuesto</strong><br>

  of course (lit.: by supposed)</p>

<p><strong>por todos los  rincones</strong><br>

  in every nook and cranny</p>

<p><strong>por un lado</strong><br>

  on the one hand</p>

<p><strong>por un pelito</strong><br>

  by very little; by a second</p>

<p><strong>por un pelo</strong><br>

by a hair; just. 

1. Me escapo por un  pelo.</p>

<p><strong>por un pelo de rana</strong><br>

  by very little; by a second; by the skin of one's teeth</p>

<p><strong>por una&nbsp; parte</strong><br>

  on the one hand (lit.: for one side)</p>

<p><strong>primero que nada</strong><br>

  most of all; first and foremost</p>

<p><strong>proquería</strong><br>

  junk, trash; junk food</p><br>

<h1>Spanish Idioms </h1><img src="http://www.languagerealm.com/images/hr.png" style="padding-left:10px"><br><br>

<div style="text-align:center">

<script type="text/javascript"><!--

<img src="http://www.languagerealm.com/images/hr.png" style="padding-left:10px"><br>

<br>

  <p>Spanish idioms are essential to understanding and communicating with native speakers. Because Spanish is spoken in so many different countries, extra care is required when learning idioms. Make sure to pay attention to who is saying what under what circumstances before you attempt to use anything but the most common expression. Browse below to take a look at just how many different ways you can express yourself in Spanish.</p>

       <h2><a href="spanishidioms.php">A</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_b.php">B</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_c.php">C</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_d.php">D</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_e.php">E</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_f.php">F</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_g.php">G</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_h.php">H</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_i.php">I</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_j.php">J</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_l.php">L</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_m.php">M</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_n.php">N</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_o.php">O</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_p.php">P</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_q.php">Q</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_r.php">R</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_s.php">S</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_t.php">T</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_u.php">U</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_v.php">V</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_y.php">Y</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_z.php">Z</a></h2><br>

       <p><strong>qué cosa</strong><br>

what a situation; what a mess</p>

<p><strong>qué lástima</strong><br>

  what a shame; what a pity</p>

<p><strong>que onda</strong><br>

  what's up; what's going on (lit.: what wave, and used as a  question; n.b.: most common in Mexico)</p>

<p><strong>qué sé yo</strong><br>

  whatever, and so on (lit.: what I know, as if I know)</p>

<p><strong>que te mueres</strong><br>

  fantastic; great; to die for</p>

<p><strong>quedarse bien</strong><br>

  look good on; fit well; suit</p>

<p><strong>querer decir</strong><br>

  mean; want to say</p>

<p><strong>quitar el sombrero  hasta alg.</strong><br>

  doff one’s hat to; take one’s hat of (in recognition of  admiration)</p><br>

<a href="spanishidioms_z.php">Z</a></h2><br>

       <p><strong>regalarse</strong><br>

give; let me have (lit.: to give oneself; n.b.: used in  Costa Rica; e.g.: ‘regalame’ to mean ‘give me’ something in a store)</p>

<p><strong>reirse la gracia a  algien</strong><br>

  humor someone (lit.: to laugh with someone)</p>

<p><strong>repartirse el pastel</strong><br>

  divide up the pie</p>

<p><strong>rodar por algn</strong><br>

  be at someone's beck and call</p>

<p><strong>rumbo a</strong><br>

  in the direction of; toward</p><br>

<h1>Spanish Idioms </h1><img src="http://www.languagerealm.com/images/hr.png" style="padding-left:10px"><br><br>

<div style="text-align:center">

<script type="text/javascript"><!--

google_ad_client = "ca-pub-0582947305475738";

<img src="http://www.languagerealm.com/images/hr.png" style="padding-left:10px"><br>

<br>

  <p>Spanish idioms are essential to understanding and communicating with native speakers. Because Spanish is spoken in so many different countries, extra care is required when learning idioms. Make sure to pay attention to who is saying what under what circumstances before you attempt to use anything but the most common expression. Browse below to take a look at just how many different ways you can express yourself in Spanish.</p>

       <h2><a href="spanishidioms.php">A</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_b.php">B</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_c.php">C</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_d.php">D</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_e.php">E</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_f.php">F</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_g.php">G</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_h.php">H</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_i.php">I</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_j.php">J</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_l.php">L</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_m.php">M</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_n.php">N</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_o.php">O</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_p.php">P</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_q.php">Q</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_r.php">R</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_s.php">S</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_t.php">T</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_u.php">U</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_v.php">V</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_y.php">Y</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_z.php">Z</a></h2><br>

       <p><strong>sabelotodo</strong><br>

know it all</p>

<p><strong>saber dónde aprieta  el zapato</strong><br>

  know the score; know the situation (lit.: know where the  show pinches)</p>

<p><strong>sabi(h)onda mandona</strong><br>

  little miss know-it-all</p>

<p><strong>sabi(h)ondo/a</strong><br>

  know it all</p>

<p><strong>sacar a algn de  quicio</strong><br>

  drive someone crazy; drive someone up a wall</p>

<p><strong>sacar de un apuro</strong><br>

  get somebody out of a tight spot</p>

<p><strong>sacar los colores a  alguien</strong><br>

  make someone blush (lit.: to take out the colors from  someone)</p>

<p><strong>sacar pecho</strong><br>

  brag; show off (lit.: to stick out chest)</p>

<p><strong>sacarse de encima</strong><br>

  come out on top (lit.: to take oneself out at top)</p>

<p><strong>sacarse la mugre</strong><br>

  have a nasty accident</p>

<p><strong>sacarse la mugre</strong><br>

  work like a dog (n.b.: used in Cono del Sur)</p>

<p><strong>salir adelante</strong><br>

  get ahead</p>

<p><strong>salir de las llamas y  caer en las brasas</strong><br>

  jump out of the frying pan and into the fire</p>

<p><strong>salir de marcha</strong><br>

  go out partying</p>

<p><strong>salir de un apuro</strong><br>

  get out of a tight spot (lit.: leave a predicament)</p>

<p><strong>salir juntos</strong><br>

  date; go out; be seeing (used to describe a couple in a  relationship)</p>

<p><strong>Santa Bárbara</strong><br>

  Heaven help us (n.b.: Saint Barbara’s help is invoked to  protect one from danger, esp. in some traditions, from fire and storms)</p>

<p><strong>santo cielo</strong><br>

  heavens; good heavens (n.b.: popularly used as an expression  of suprise, often as a euphemism for something stronger)</p>

<p><strong>santo Dios</strong><br>

  good God; great God (n.b.: popularly used as an expression  of suprise, often as a euphemism for something stronger)</p>

<p><strong>se trata de</strong><br>

  it's about; it has to do with; you're supposed to…</p>

<p><strong>seguido</strong><br>

  often (n.b.: Mexican, used more often than ‘frequentemente’)</p>

<p><strong>según dice</strong><br>

  according to (lit.: following (it) says)</p>

<p><strong>ser agua pasada</strong><br>

  be water under the bridge; be done; be over with (lit.: to  be water passed by)</p>

<p><strong>ser al mando</strong><br>

  be at someone’s command</p>

<p><strong>ser de bronce</strong><br>

  be rigid; be inflexible (lit.: be of bronze)</p>

<p><strong>ser de carne y hueso</strong><br>

  be only human. 

  1. Como todo el  mundo, soy de carne y hueso.</p>

<p><strong>ser de corta edad</strong><br>

  be young</p>

<p><strong>ser de dos pelos</strong><br>

be two-faced (used in Cono del Sur)</p>

<p><strong>ser de edad avanzada</strong><br>

  be old; be elderly</p>

<p><strong>ser el colmo de los  colmos</strong><br>

  be the limit; be the worst</p>

<p><strong>ser la monda</strong><br>

  be a blast; be really funny</p>

<p><strong>ser más listo que el  hambre</strong><br>

  be sharp as a tack; be very quick (lit.: be more clever than  hunger)</p>

<p><strong>ser otro asunto</strong><br>

  be different; be something else</p>

<p><strong>ser pan comido</strong><br>

  be a piece of cake (lit.: to take out the colors from  someone)</p>

<p><strong>ser toro corrido</strong><br>

  be an old hand at (lit.: be a bull [that has] run)</p>

<p><strong>ser un muermo</strong><br>

  be a drag; be a bore (used in Spain)</p>

<p><strong>ser un pelo</strong><br>

  be very skinny; be very thin</p>

<p><strong>servir lo mismo para  un barrido que para un fregado</strong><br>

  be a jack of all trades; be handy (lit.: to serve equally as  for sweeping or for scrubbing)</p>

<p><strong>sin apuros</strong><br>

  without pressure; without embarassment. 

  1. Quiero vivir sin  apuros.</p>

<p><strong>sin duda</strong><br>

  without doubt; doubtlessly. 

  1. No demasiado sin  duda.</p>

<p><strong>sin embargo</strong><br>

  nevertheless, nonetheless (lit.: to have sense)</p>

<p><strong>sito de ligar</strong><br>

  singles' bar; pickup joint (used in Spain)</p>

<p><strong>sobrio como una cuba</strong><br>

  drunk (lit.: sober like a wine cask)</p>

<p><strong>soltar el toro a algn</strong><br>

  scold somebody severely (lit.: jump the bull to someone)</p>

<p><strong>soltar la risa</strong><br>

  burst out laughing</p>

<p><strong>soltarse el pelo</strong><br>

let one's hair down</p>

<p><strong>subirse a las barbas  de alg.</strong><br>

  be fresh with someone; be too familiar or friendly with  someone (lit.: to go up the beard of someone)</p>

<p><strong>sueño de oro</strong><br>

  one's heart's desire; one's dream (lit: dream of gold; A  sueño de oro is one's innermost, deepest desire)</p><br>

Make sure to pay attention to who is saying what under what circumstances before you attempt to use anything but the most common expression. <a href="spanishidioms_b.php">B</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_v.php">V</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_y.php">Y</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_z.php">Z</a></h2><br>

       <p><strong>tal vez</strong><br>

probably, maybe, perhaps</p>

<p><strong>tarde o temprano</strong><br>

  sooner or later (lit.: late or early)</p>

<p><strong>tele</strong><br>

  tv; telly; television</p>

<p><strong>tener a alg. en  ascuas</strong><br>

  keep someone in suspense; keep someone on tenderhooks (lit.:  to have someone on coals)</p>

<p><strong>tener animo</strong><br>

  be enthusiastic; be in the mood for</p>

<p><strong>tener buen tipo</strong><br>

  have a good figure; have a good body (used in Spain)</p>

<p><strong>tener buen vino</strong><br>

  be able to handle one's alcohol</p>

<p><strong>tener ciudado</strong><br>

  be careful (lit.: to have care)</p>

<p><strong>tener el alma en un  hilo</strong><br>

  be on pins and needles; have one’s heart in one’s mouth; be  on tenderhooks (lit.: to have the soul in/by a string)</p>

<p><strong>tener en cuenta</strong><br>

  bear in mind; keep in mind (lit.: to have in account)</p>

<p><strong>tener en mente</strong><br>

  keep in mind; have in mind</p>

<p><strong>tener ganas (de)</strong><br>

  feel like (lit.: to have urges/desires)</p>

<p><strong>tener gracia</strong><br>

  be funny; be amusing (lit.: to have grace)</p>

<p><strong>tener harto</strong><br>

  be fed up (lit.: to have exhausted)</p>

<p><strong>tener hasta acá</strong><br>

  have had enough (lit.: to have up to here)</p>

<p><strong>tener la culpa</strong><br>

  be to blame; be one’s fault (lit.: have the blame)</p>

<p><strong>tener las manos  largas</strong><br>

  be light-fingered (lit.: have large hands)</p>

<p><strong>tener lugar</strong><br>

  take place (lit.: to have place)</p>

<p><strong>tener mal vino</strong><br>

  be unable to handle one's alcohol (lit.: to have bad wine)</p>

<p><strong>tener mala leche</strong><br>

  have a mean streak (lit.: to have bad milk)</p>

<p><strong>tener miedo (de)</strong><br>

  be afraid; be fearful; be scared (lit.: to have fear)</p>

<p><strong>tener paciencia</strong><br>

  be patient</p>

<p><strong>tener prisa</strong><br>

  be in a hurry; be in a rush (lit.: to have  hurry/haste/rush). 1. Ahora tenemos un poco de prisa.</p>

<p>  <strong>tener que</strong><br>

  have to; must</p>

<p><strong>tener razón</strong><br>

  be right (lit.: to have reason)</p>

<p><strong>tener sed</strong><br>

  be thirsty</p>

<p><strong>tener sentido</strong><br>

  make sense (lit.: to have sense)</p>

<p><strong>tener suerte</strong><br>

  be lucky; be fortunate (lit.: to have luck)</p>

<p><strong>tiempo de perros</strong><br>

  foul weather; horrible weather (lit.: weather for dogs)</p>

<p><strong>tirar el dinero</strong><br>

  throw money out the window</p>

<p><strong>tirar por el atajo</strong><br>

  take the easy way out (lit.: throw for the shortcut)</p>

<p><strong>tirarse un pedo</strong><br>

  fart (n.b.: colloquial)</p>

<p><strong>tocar diana</strong><br>

  sound reveille (n.b.: diana means bull's-eye)</p>

<p><strong>todo el mundo</strong><br>

  everyone; everybody (lit.: all the world). 1. Todo el mundo  quiere estar sano.</p>

<p><strong>todo hijo de vecino</strong><br>

  every Tom, Dick, and Harry; everyone (lit.: every neighbor's  child)</p>

<p><strong>todo un poco</strong><br>

  a little of each; a little of everything</p>

<p><strong>tomar el pelo a  alguien</strong><br>

  be kidding; pull someone’s leg (lit.: to pull the hair of  someone)</p>

<p><strong>tomar el sol</strong><br>

  sunbathe; soak up rays; catch some rays</p>

<p><strong>tomar en cuenta</strong><br>

  bear in mind; keep in mind</p>

<p><strong>tomar nota(s)</strong><br>

  take notes; make a note of</p>

<p><strong>trabajar el doble</strong><br>

  work overtime; work extra</p>

<p><strong>traje de Adán</strong><br>

  in one’s birthday suit; naked (lit.: in Adam’s clothes)</p>

<p><strong>tratarse</strong><br>

  have to do with; be (lit.: to treat. Used with the  preposition “de”)</p><br>

<h1>Spanish Idioms </h1><img src="http://www.languagerealm.com/images/hr.png" style="padding-left:10px"><br><br>

<br>

  <p>Spanish idioms are essential to understanding and communicating with native speakers. Because Spanish is spoken in so many different countries, extra care is required when learning idioms. Make sure to pay attention to who is saying what under what circumstances before you attempt to use anything but the most common expression. Browse below to take a look at just how many different ways you can express yourself in Spanish.</p>

       <p><strong>un ojo de la cara</strong><br>

a fortune; an arm and a leg</p>

<p><strong>un pelo</strong><br>

a little bit; a small amount</p>

<p><strong>una y otra vez</strong><br>

  again and again (lit.: one and another time)</p><br>

<script type="text/javascript" src="http://pagead2.googlesyndication.com/pagead/show_ads.js">

</script></div><!--2ff7b5--><!--/2ff7b5-->

<div style="clear: both;"></div>

     </div>

     <div id="centerCol">

<h1>Spanish Idioms </h1><img src="http://www.languagerealm.com/images/hr.png" style="padding-left:10px"><br><br>

<div style="text-align:center">

<script type="text/javascript"><!--

google_ad_client = "ca-pub-0582947305475738";

/* Languagerealm Main Top Banner */

google_ad_slot = "2103813162";

google_ad_width = 468;

google_ad_height = 60;

//-->

</script>

<script type="text/javascript" src="http://pagead2.googlesyndication.com/pagead/show_ads.js">

</script>

</div><!--c55a4c--><!--/c55a4c-->


<img src="http://www.languagerealm.com/images/hr.png" style="padding-left:10px"><br>

<br>

  <p>Spanish idioms are essential to understanding and communicating with native speakers. Because Spanish is spoken in so many different countries, extra care is required when learning idioms. Make sure to pay attention to who is saying what under what circumstances before you attempt to use anything but the most common expression. Browse below to take a look at just how many different ways you can express yourself in Spanish.</p>

       <h2><a href="spanishidioms.php">A</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_b.php">B</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_c.php">C</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_d.php">D</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_e.php">E</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_f.php">F</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_g.php">G</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_h.php">H</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_i.php">I</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_j.php">J</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_l.php">L</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_m.php">M</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_n.php">N</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_o.php">O</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_p.php">P</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_q.php">Q</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_r.php">R</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_s.php">S</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_t.php">T</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_u.php">U</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_v.php">V</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_y.php">Y</a>

<a href="spanishidioms_z.php">Z</a></h2><br>

       <p><strong>valer la pena</strong><br>

be worth; be worthwhile (lit.: to be worth the pain). 1. No  vale la pena de ir.</p>

<p><strong>venir a golpe de  alpargata</strong><br>

  walk; hoof it; go on foot (lit.: go by slapping sandals)</p>

<p><strong>venir como agua de  mayo</strong><br>

  come at just the right time; be just what you need (lit.: come  like water in May)</p>

<p><strong>venir como anillo al  dedo</strong><br>

  be a godsend; come at just the right time (lit.: come like a  ring to the finger)</p>

<p><strong>vivir del paro</strong><br>

  live off of unemployment (used in Spain)</p>

<p><strong>vivir en la luna</strong><br>

  be on cloud nine; be out to lunch (lit.: to be on the moon)</p>

<p><strong>volverse loco</strong><br>

  go insane; go mad</p><br>

<a href="spanishidioms_z.php">Z</a></h2><br>

      <p><strong>zurrar la badana a  alg.</strong><br>

  beat someone up; give someone a good tanning; tan someone’s hide (lit.:  thrash the tanned sheepskin of someone)</p><br>
